<p>In February 2014, the opposition groups of the Islamic Front claimed responsibility for destroying a series of major historic buildings in the old city including the justice palace, the Carlton Citadel hotel which was being used as an army base,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> the old building of the city council, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Serail_of_Aleppo" title="Grand Serail of Aleppo">Grand Serail of Aleppo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khusruwiyah_Mosque" title="Khusruwiyah Mosque">Khusruwiyah Mosque</a>, Khan al-Shouneh and many other souqs and khans.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 August 2016, a report for a <a href="/wiki/Richard_A._Falk#In_human_rights_groups" title="Richard A. Falk">Euro-Med Monitor</a> team confirmed that one of the hospitals, overcrowded by injured civilians, was bombarded by Russian warplanes in the western Aleppo countryside, which, according to Euro-Med Monitor, is a very clear violation of the international laws saying that those civilians must be protected from the continuing conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>A stalemate that had been in place for four years finally ended in July 2016, when Syrian government troops closed the last supply line of the armed opposition into Aleppo with the support of Russian airstrikes. In response, rebel forces launched unsuccessful counteroffensives in September and October that failed to break the siege; in November, government forces embarked on a decisive campaign that resulted in the recapture of all of Aleppo in December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The Syrian government victory was widely seen as a potential turning point in Syria's civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> On December 25, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> was celebrated in Aleppo for the first time in four years.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D8%AA%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%84_%D8%AC%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%AD%D9%84%D8%A8.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/%D8%AA%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%84_%D8%AC%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%AD%D9%84%D8%A8.JPG/220px-%D8%AA%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%84_%D8%AC%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%AD%D9%84%D8%A8.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/%D8%AA%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%84_%D8%AC%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%AD%D9%84%D8%A8.JPG/330px-%D8%AA%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%84_%D8%AC%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%AD%D9%84%D8%A8.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/%D8%AA%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%84_%D8%AC%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%AD%D9%84%D8%A8.JPG/440px-%D8%AA%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%84_%D8%AC%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%AD%D9%84%D8%A8.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D8%AA%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%84_%D8%AC%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%AD%D9%84%D8%A8.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The nearby <a href="/wiki/Kurd_Mountains" title="Kurd Mountains">Kurd Mountains</a> at the northwest of Aleppo</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Aleppo,_Queik_river_at_night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Downtown_Aleppo%2C_Queik_river_at_night.jpg/220px-Downtown_Aleppo%2C_Queik_river_at_night.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Downtown_Aleppo%2C_Queik_river_at_night.jpg/330px-Downtown_Aleppo%2C_Queik_river_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Downtown_Aleppo%2C_Queik_river_at_night.jpg/440px-Downtown_Aleppo%2C_Queik_river_at_night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="731" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Aleppo,_Queik_river_at_night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Queiq_River" title="Queiq River">Queiq River</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aleppo lies about 120&#160;km (75&#160;mi) inland from the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, on a <a href="/wiki/Aleppo_plateau" title="Aleppo plateau">plateau</a> 380&#160;m (1,250&#160;ft) above sea level, 45&#160;km (28&#160;mi) east of the Syrian-Turkish border <a href="/wiki/Bab_al-Hawa_Border_Crossing" title="Bab al-Hawa Border Crossing">checkpoint of Bab al-Hawa</a>. The city is surrounded by farmlands from the north and the west, widely cultivated with olive and <a href="/wiki/Pistachio" title="Pistachio">pistachio</a> trees. To the east, Aleppo approaches the dry areas of the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Desert" title="Syrian Desert">Syrian Desert</a>.</p>
<p>The city was founded a few kilometres south of the location of the current old city, on the right bank of <a href="/wiki/Queiq_River" title="Queiq River">Queiq River</a> which arises from the <a href="/wiki/Aintab_plateau" title="Aintab plateau">Aintab plateau</a> in the north and runs through Aleppo southward to the fertile country of <a href="/wiki/Qinnasrin" title="Qinnasrin">Qinnasrin</a>. The old city of Aleppo lies on the left bank of the Queiq. It was surrounded by a circle of eight hills surrounding a prominent central hill on which the castle (originally a temple dating to the 2nd millennium BC) was erected. The radius of the circle is about 10&#160;km (6.2&#160;mi). The hills are Tell as-Sawda, Tell ʕāysha, Tell as-Sett, Tell al-Yāsmīn (Al-ʕaqaba), Tell al-Ansāri (Yārūqiyya), ʕan at-Tall, al-Jallūm, Baḥsīta.<sup id="cite_ref-Duden6_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Duden6-98">[98]</a></sup> The old city was enclosed within an ancient wall that was last rebuilt by the <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluks</a>. The wall has since disappeared. It had nine gates and was surrounded by a broad deep ditch.<sup id="cite_ref-Duden6_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Duden6-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>Occupying an area of more than 190&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (73&#160;sq&#160;mi), Aleppo is one of the fastest growing cities in the Middle East. According to the new major plan of the city adopted in 2001, it is envisaged to increase the total area of Aleppo up to 420&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (160&#160;sq&#160;mi) by the end of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Syr-news1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syr-news1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aleppo_plan_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aleppo_plan-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aleppo has a <a href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Cold semi-arid climate">cool steppe climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: BSk). The mountain series that run along the Mediterranean coast, namely <a href="/wiki/Mount_Alawites" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Alawites">Mount Alawites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Amanus" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Amanus">Mount Amanus</a>, largely block the effects of the Mediterranean on climate (<a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow_effect" class="mw-redirect" title="Rain shadow effect">rain shadow effect</a>). The average high and low temperature throughout the year is 23.8 and 11.1&#160;°C (74.8 and 52.0&#160;°F). The average precipitation is 329.4&#160;mm (12.97&#160;in). More than 80% of precipitation occurs between October and March. Snow one or two times every winter. Average humidity is 55.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alepp0fashion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Alepp0fashion.jpg/170px-Alepp0fashion.jpg" width="170" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Alepp0fashion.jpg/255px-Alepp0fashion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Alepp0fashion.jpg/340px-Alepp0fashion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2030" data-file-height="2010" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alepp0fashion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> woman and a couple of <a href="/wiki/Bedouins" class="mw-redirect" title="Bedouins">Bedouins</a> in Aleppo, 1873</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the Aleppine historian Sheikh <i>Kamel Al-Ghazzi</i> (1853–1933), the population of Aleppo was around 400,000 before the disastrous earthquake of 1822. Followed by cholera and plague attacks in 1823 and 1827 respectively, the population of the city declined to 110,000 by the end of the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> In 1901, the total population of Aleppo was 108,143 of which Muslims were 76,329 (70.58%), Christians – mostly Catholics – 24,508 (22.66%) and Jews 7,306 (6.76%).<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aleppo's large Christian population swelled with the influx of <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Syria" title="Armenians in Syria">Armenian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assyrians_in_Syria" class="mw-redirect" title="Assyrians in Syria">Assyrian-Syriac</a> Christian refugees during the early 20th-century and after the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Assyrian Genocide">Assyrian</a> genocides of 1915. After the arrival of the first groups of <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Syria" title="Armenians in Syria">Armenian</a> refugees (1915–1922) the population of Aleppo in 1922 counted 156,748 of which Muslims were 97,600 (62.26%), native Christians -mostly Catholics- 22,117 (14.11%), Jews 6,580 (4.20%), Europeans 2,652 (1.70%), Armenian refugees 20,007 (12.76%) and others 7,792 (4.97%).<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> However, even though a large majority of the Armenians arrived during the period, the city has had an Armenian community since at least the 1100s, when a considerable number of Armenian families and merchants from the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Kingdom_of_Cilicia" title="Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia">Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia</a> settled in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Forty_Martyrs_Cathedral" title="Forty Martyrs Cathedral">oldest Armenian church in the city</a> is from 1491 as well, which indicates that they have been here long before.</p>
<p>The second period of Armenian flow towards Aleppo marked with the withdrawal of the French troops from <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">Cilicia</a> in 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> After the arrival of more than 40,000 Armenian refugees between 1923 and 1925, the population of the city reached up to 210,000 by the end of 1925, where Armenians formed more than 25% of it.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the historical data presented by <i>Al-Ghazzi</i>, the vast majority of the Aleppine Christians were Catholics until the latter days of the Ottoman rule. The growth of the <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodox">Oriental Orthodox</a> Christians is related with the arrival of the Assyrian survivors from Cilicia and Southern Turkey, while on the other hand, large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church_of_Antioch" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox Church of Antioch">Eastern Orthodox Christians</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Hatay_Province" title="Hatay Province">Sanjak of Alexandretta</a> arrived in Aleppo, after the annexation of the Sanjak in 1939 in favour of Turkey.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Umayyad_Mosque,_Aleppo,_Syria_(5077865830).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Umayyad_Mosque%2C_Aleppo%2C_Syria_%285077865830%29.jpg/220px-Umayyad_Mosque%2C_Aleppo%2C_Syria_%285077865830%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Umayyad_Mosque%2C_Aleppo%2C_Syria_%285077865830%29.jpg/330px-Umayyad_Mosque%2C_Aleppo%2C_Syria_%285077865830%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Umayyad_Mosque%2C_Aleppo%2C_Syria_%285077865830%29.jpg/440px-Umayyad_Mosque%2C_Aleppo%2C_Syria_%285077865830%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Umayyad_Mosque,_Aleppo,_Syria_(5077865830).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Syrian children in Aleppo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1944, Aleppo's population was around 325,000, with 112,110 (34.5%) Christians among which Armenians have counted 60,200. Armenians formed more than half of the Christian community in Aleppo until 1947, when many groups of them left for <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Armenia">Soviet Armenia</a> within the frames of the <i>Armenian Repatriation Process (1946–1967)</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-civil_war_status">Pre-civil war status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Pre-civil war status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

</tr>
</table>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rahman_mosque.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Rahman_mosque.jpg/220px-Rahman_mosque.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Rahman_mosque.jpg/330px-Rahman_mosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Rahman_mosque.jpg/440px-Rahman_mosque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1138" data-file-height="889" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rahman_mosque.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ar-Rahman_Mosque" title="Ar-Rahman Mosque">Ar-Rahman Mosque</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aleppo is the most populous city in Syria, with a population of 2,132,100 as indicated in the latest official census in 2004 by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bureau_of_Statistics_(Syria)" title="Central Bureau of Statistics (Syria)">Syria Central Bureau of Statistics</a> (CBS). Its subdistrict (<i><a href="/wiki/Nahiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Nahiya">nahiya</a></i>) consists of 23 localities with a collective population of 2,181,061 in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-CBS_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS-110">[110]</a></sup> According to the official estimate announced by the Aleppo City Council, the population of the city was 2,301,570 by the end of 2005. As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a>, however, the city eastern half's population under the control of the opposition had plummeted to an estimated 40,000 by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Arabic-speaking population of Aleppo uses the <a href="/wiki/North_Syrian_Arabic" title="North Syrian Arabic">North Syrian dialect</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Levantine_Arabic" title="Levantine Arabic">Levantine Arabic</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Muslims">Muslims</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Muslims">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>More than 80% of Aleppo's inhabitants are <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> <a href="/wiki/Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>. They are mainly <a href="/wiki/Syrian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian people">Arabs</a> followed by <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Turkmen" title="Syrian Turkmen">Turkmens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>. Other Muslim groups include small numbers of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chechens" title="Chechens">Chechens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>.</p>
<p>The northwestern districts of Aleppo, in particular the Sheikh Maqsoud district, are the Kurdish sections of the city. Since the start of the civil war in Syria, these districts of Aleppo are protected by Kurdish militias and are thus, the safest districts of Aleppo. Neither the central government forces or the rebel armies have challenged the Kurdish military nor encroached into those Kurdish districts. Many non-Kurds of Aleppo have fled into the safety of the Kurdish district for protection. Kurds constituted about 7–10% of the city population before the war.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christians">Christians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Christians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Surp_Asdvadzadzin10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Surp_Asdvadzadzin10.jpg/220px-Surp_Asdvadzadzin10.jpg" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Surp_Asdvadzadzin10.jpg/330px-Surp_Asdvadzadzin10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Surp_Asdvadzadzin10.jpg/440px-Surp_Asdvadzadzin10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1613" data-file-height="1343" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Surp_Asdvadzadzin10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Mother_of_God_(Aleppo)" title="Church of the Holy Mother of God (Aleppo)">Armenian Apostolic church of the Holy Mother of God</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As one of the largest Christian communities in the Middle East, Aleppo is home to many <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodox">Oriental Orthodox</a> Christian congregations, mainly <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Syria" title="Armenians in Syria">Armenians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assyrians_in_Syria" class="mw-redirect" title="Assyrians in Syria">Assyrians/Syriacs</a>. Historically, the city is the main centre of French Catholic Missionaries in Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Nowadays, more than 250,000 Christians live in the city representing about 12% of the total population, though the flight of refugees from the city as a result of the Syrian Civil War has led to the Christian population still in Aleppo falling to only 100,000, of whom half are ethnic <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Syria" title="Armenians in Syria">Armenians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> A significant number of <a href="/wiki/Assyrians_in_Syria" class="mw-redirect" title="Assyrians in Syria">Assyrians</a> in Aleppo speak <a href="/wiki/Aramaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Aramaic">Aramaic</a> and hail from the city of <a href="/wiki/Urfa" class="mw-redirect" title="Urfa">Urfa</a> in Turkey. The large community of <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodox">Oriental Orthodox</a> Christians belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Orthodox_Church" title="Syriac Orthodox Church">Syriac Orthodox</a> churches. Also, there are members of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church_of_Antioch" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox Church of Antioch">Eastern Orthodox Church of Antioch</a>. There is also a strong presence of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Catholic">Eastern Catholic</a> Christians in the city including <a href="/wiki/Melkite_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Melkite Catholic Church">Melkite Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Church">Maronite Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaldean_Catholic_Church" title="Chaldean Catholic Church">Chaldean Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Catholic_Church" title="Syriac Catholic Church">Syriac Catholics</a> and also there are some who follow the <a href="/wiki/Latin_rite" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin rite">Latin rite</a>. <a href="/wiki/Evangelical" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical">Evangelical</a> Christians of different denominations are a minority in the city. Several areas have a Christian and Armenian majority, such as the old Christian quarter of <a href="/wiki/Al-Jdayde" title="Al-Jdayde">Jdeydeh</a>. Currently, there are 45 operating churches in the city, possessed by the above-mentioned Christian congregations.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jews">Jews</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Jews">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Synagogue_Aleppo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Synagogue_Aleppo.jpg/220px-Synagogue_Aleppo.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Synagogue_Aleppo.jpg/330px-Synagogue_Aleppo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Synagogue_Aleppo.jpg/440px-Synagogue_Aleppo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="958" data-file-height="583" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Synagogue_Aleppo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Central synagogue in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city was home to a significant <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> population from ancient times. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Synagogue_of_Aleppo" title="Central Synagogue of Aleppo">Great Synagogue</a>, built in the 5th century, housed the <a href="/wiki/Aleppo_Codex" title="Aleppo Codex">Aleppo Codex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The Jews of Aleppo were known for their religious commitment, Rabbinic leadership, and their liturgy, consisting of <a href="/wiki/Pizmonim" title="Pizmonim">Pizmonim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baqashot" title="Baqashot">Baqashot</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a>, the city of Aleppo received many Sephardic Jewish immigrants, who eventually joined with the native Aleppo Jewish community. Peaceful relations existed between the Jews and surrounding population. In the early 20th-century, the town's Jews lived mainly in Al-Jamiliyah, Bab Al-Faraj and the neighbourhoods around the Great Synagogue. Unrest in Palestine in the years preceding the establishment of Israel in 1948 resulted in growing hostility towards Jews living in Arab countries, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_Arab_lands" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish exodus from Arab lands">Jewish exodus from Arab lands</a>. In December 1947, after the UN decided the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Palestine" class="mw-redirect" title="Partition of Palestine">partition of Palestine</a>, an Arab mob<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aleppo_pogrom" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleppo pogrom">attacked the Jewish quarter</a>. Homes, schools and shops were badly damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_rights_in_Syria_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_rights_in_Syria-116">[116]</a></sup> Soon after, many of the town's remaining 6,000 Jews emigrated.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.co.uk_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.co.uk-117">[117]</a></sup> In 1968, there were an estimated 700 Jews still remaining in Aleppo.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>The houses and other properties of the Jewish families which were not sold after the migration, remain uninhabited under the protection of the Syrian Government. Most of these properties are in Al-Jamiliyah and Bab Al-Faraj areas, and the neighbourhoods around the <a href="/wiki/Central_Synagogue_of_Aleppo" title="Central Synagogue of Aleppo">Central Synagogue of Aleppo</a>. In 1992, the Syrian government lifted the travel ban on its 4,500 Jewish citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Most traveled to the United States, where a sizable number of <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Jews" title="Syrian Jews">Syrian Jews</a> currently live in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York. The last Jews of Aleppo, the Halabi family, were evacuated from the city in October 2016 by the <a href="/wiki/Free_Syrian_Army" title="Free Syrian Army">Free Syrian Army</a> and now live in Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Jews from Aleppo referred to their city as "Aram Tzova" (ארם צובא) after the ancient <a href="/wiki/Aramean" class="mw-redirect" title="Aramean">Aramean</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Aram-Zobah" class="mw-redirect" title="Aram-Zobah">Aram-Zobah</a> mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">Hebrew Bible</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_citadel_Museum_laz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Aleppo_citadel_Museum_laz.jpg/220px-Aleppo_citadel_Museum_laz.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Aleppo_citadel_Museum_laz.jpg/330px-Aleppo_citadel_Museum_laz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Aleppo_citadel_Museum_laz.jpg/440px-Aleppo_citadel_Museum_laz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_citadel_Museum_laz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Aleppo_Citadel_Museum" title="Aleppo Citadel Museum">Aleppo Citadel Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Aleppo" title="National Museum of Aleppo">National Museum of Aleppo</a>.</li>
<li>Museum of the popular traditions known as the <i>Aleppine House</i> at <i><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Ajikbash_House" class="extiw" title="commons:Category:Ajikbash House">Beit Achiqbash</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Al-Jdayde" title="Al-Jdayde">Jdeydeh</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aleppo_Citadel_Museum" title="Aleppo Citadel Museum">Aleppo Citadel Museum</a>.</li>

<li><i>Zarehian Treasury</i> of the Armenian Apostolic Church at the old Armenian church of the Holy Mother of God, <a href="/wiki/Al-Jdayde" title="Al-Jdayde">Jdeydeh</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppomusic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Aleppomusic.jpg/220px-Aleppomusic.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Aleppomusic.jpg/330px-Aleppomusic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Aleppomusic.jpg/440px-Aleppomusic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="556" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppomusic.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Musicians from Aleppo, 18th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aleppo is considered one of the main centres of Arabic traditional and classic music with the famous Aleppine <i><a href="/wiki/Muwashshah" title="Muwashshah">Muwashshahs</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Qudud_Halabiya" title="Qudud Halabiya">Qudud Halabiya</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Arabic_maqam" title="Arabic maqam">Maqams</a></i> (religious, secular and folk poetic-musical genres). Aleppines in general are fond of Arab classical music, the <i>Tarab</i>, and it is not a surprise that many artists from Aleppo are considered pioneers among the Arabs in classic and traditional music. The most prominent figures in this field are Sabri Mdallal, <a href="/wiki/Sabah_Fakhri" title="Sabah Fakhri">Sabah Fakhri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shadi_Jamil" title="Shadi Jamil">Shadi Jamil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abed_Azrie" title="Abed Azrie">Abed Azrie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nour_Mhanna" title="Nour Mhanna">Nour Mhanna</a>. Many iconic artists of the Arab music like <a href="/wiki/Sayed_Darwish" title="Sayed Darwish">Sayed Darwish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Abdel_Wahab" title="Mohammed Abdel Wahab">Mohammed Abdel Wahab</a> were visiting Aleppo to recognize the legacy of Aleppine art and learn from its cultural heritage.</p>
<p>Aleppo is also known for its knowledgeable and cultivated listeners, known as <i>sammi'a</i> or "connoisseur listeners".<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Aleppine musicians often claim that no major Arab artist achieved fame without first earning the approval of the Aleppine <i>sammi'a</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aleppo hosts many music shows and festivals every year at the citadel amphitheatre, such as the "Syrian Song Festival", the "Silk Road Festival" and "Khan al-Harir Festival".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kebab_khashkhash.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Kebab_khashkhash.jpg/220px-Kebab_khashkhash.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Kebab_khashkhash.jpg/330px-Kebab_khashkhash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/71/Kebab_khashkhash.jpg 2x" data-file-width="336" data-file-height="247" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kebab_khashkhash.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kebab khashkhash from Aleppo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Syrian_cuisine" title="Syrian cuisine">Syrian cuisine</a> in general, and especially Aleppine cuisine, has a very wide selection of dishes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="If Aleppine cuisine is a subset of Syrian cuisine, then how can &quot;especially Aleppine cuisine&quot; have a wide selection of dishes? Surely, by definition, it has a less wide selection than, or at most just as wide a selection as, Syrian cuisine overall. (December 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Being surrounded by olive, nut and fruit orchards, Aleppo is famous for a love of eating, as the cuisine is the product of fertile land and location along the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>. The International Academy of Gastronomy in France awarded Aleppo its culinary prize in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> But in fact, Aleppo was a food capital long before Paris, because of its diverse communities of <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a>, Arab Christian and <a href="/wiki/Turcomans" class="mw-redirect" title="Turcomans">Turcomans</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> All of those groups contributed food traditions, since Aleppo was part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The city has a vast selection of different types of dishes, such as <a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">kebab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kibbeh" title="Kibbeh">kibbeh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolma" title="Dolma">dolma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hummus" title="Hummus">hummus</a>, ful halabi, <a href="/wiki/Za%27atar" title="Za'atar">za'atar</a> halabi, etc. Ful halabi is a typical Aleppine breakfast meal: fava bean soup with a splash of olive oil, lemon juice, garlic and Aleppo's red peppers. The za'atar of Aleppo (thyme) is a kind of oregano which is very popular in the regional cuisines.</p>
<p>The kibbeh is one of the favourite foods of the locals, and the Aleppines have created more than 17 types of kibbeh dishes, which is considered a form of art for them. These include <i>kibbeh</i> prepared with <a href="/wiki/Sumac" title="Sumac">sumac</a> (<i>kәbbe sәmmāʔiyye</i>), <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">yogurt</a> (<i>kәbbe labaniyye</i>), <a href="/wiki/Quince" title="Quince">quince</a> (<i>kәbbe safarjaliyye</i>), lemon juice (<i>kәbbe ḥāmḍa</i>), <a href="/wiki/Pomegranate" title="Pomegranate">pomegranate</a> sauce and <a href="/wiki/Cherry" title="Cherry">cherry</a> sauce. Other varieties include the "disk" <i>kibbeh</i> (<i>kәbbe ʔrāṣ</i>), the "plate" <i>kibbeh</i> (<i>kәbbe bәṣfīḥa</i> or <i>kәbbe bṣēniyye</i>) and the raw <i>kibbeh</i> (<i>kәbbe nayye</i>). Kebab Halabi -influenced by Armenian and Turkish tastes- has around 26 variants<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> including: <i>kebab</i> prepared with cherry (<i>kebab karaz</i>), eggplant (<i>kebab banjan</i>), <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chili pepper</a> with <a href="/wiki/Parsley" title="Parsley">parsley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pine_nut" title="Pine nut">pine nut</a> (<i>kebab khashkhash</i>), <a href="/wiki/Truffle" title="Truffle">truffle</a> (<i>kebab kamayeh</i>), <a href="/wiki/Tomato_paste" title="Tomato paste">tomato paste</a> (<i>kebab hindi</i>), cheese and <a href="/wiki/Mushroom" title="Mushroom">mushroom</a> (<i>kebab ma'juʔa</i>), etc.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> The favourite drink is <a href="/wiki/Arak_(distilled_beverage)" class="mw-redirect" title="Arak (distilled beverage)">Arak</a>, which is usually consumed along with <a href="/wiki/Meze" title="Meze">meze</a>, Aleppine kebabs and kibbehs. <a href="/wiki/Beer_in_Syria" title="Beer in Syria">Al-Shark beer</a> -a product of Aleppo- is also among the favourite drinks. Local wines and brandies are consumed as well.</p>
<p>Aleppo is the origin of different types of sweets and pastries. The Aleppine sweets, such as mabrumeh, siwar es-sett, balloriyyeh, etc., are characterized by containing high rates of ghee butter and sugar. Other sweets include mamuniyeh, shuaibiyyat, mushabbak, zilebiyeh, ghazel al-banat etc. Most pastries contain the renowned Aleppine pistachios and other types of nuts.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_sites">Historical sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Historical sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ancient_City_of_Aleppo" title="Ancient City of Aleppo">Ancient City of Aleppo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Citadel_of_Aleppo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Citadel_of_Aleppo.jpg/300px-Citadel_of_Aleppo.jpg" width="300" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Citadel_of_Aleppo.jpg/450px-Citadel_of_Aleppo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Citadel_of_Aleppo.jpg/600px-Citadel_of_Aleppo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1709" data-file-height="836" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Citadel_of_Aleppo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Citadel_of_Aleppo" title="Citadel of Aleppo">Aleppo Citadel</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_throne_hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Aleppo_throne_hall.jpg/220px-Aleppo_throne_hall.jpg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Aleppo_throne_hall.jpg/330px-Aleppo_throne_hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Aleppo_throne_hall.jpg/440px-Aleppo_throne_hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1712" data-file-height="2288" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_throne_hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Throne hall of the citadel</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aleppo is characterized with mixed architectural styles, having been ruled by, among others, Romans, Byzantines, Seljuqs, Mamluks and Ottomans.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Various types of 13th and 14th centuries constructions, such as caravanserais, caeserias, Quranic schools, hammams and religious buildings are found in the <a href="/wiki/Old_City_of_Aleppo" class="mw-redirect" title="Old City of Aleppo">old city</a>. The quarters of the <a href="/wiki/Al-Jdayde" title="Al-Jdayde">Jdeydeh</a> district are home to numerous 16th and 17th-century houses of the Aleppine bourgeoisie, featuring stone engravings. <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque architecture</a> of the 19th and early 20th centuries is common in the Azizyeh quarter, including the <i>Villa Rose</i>. The new ash-Shahbaa quarter is a mixture of several styles, such as <a href="/wiki/Neo-classical_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-classical architecture">Neo-classic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norman_Architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Architecture">Norman</a>, Oriental and even <a href="/wiki/Chinese_architecture" title="Chinese architecture">Chinese architecture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the old city is characterized with its large mansions, narrow alleys and covered souqs, the modern city's architecture has replenished the town with wide roads and large squares such as the <a href="/wiki/Saadallah_Al-Jabiri_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="Saadallah Al-Jabiri Square">Saadallah Al-Jabiri Square</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Square_(Aleppo)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberty Square (Aleppo)">Liberty Square</a>, the President's Square and <a href="/wiki/Sabaa_Bahrat_Square_(Aleppo)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabaa Bahrat Square (Aleppo)">Sabaa Bahrat Square</a>. There is a relatively clear division between old and new Aleppo. The older portions of the city, with an approximate area of 160 hectares (400 acres) were contained within a wall, 5&#160;km (3.1&#160;mi) in circuit with nine gates. The huge medieval <a href="/wiki/Castle" title="Castle">castle</a> in the city – known as the <a href="/wiki/Citadel_of_Aleppo" title="Citadel of Aleppo">Citadel of Aleppo</a> – occupies the center of the ancient part, in the shape of an <a href="/wiki/Acropolis" title="Acropolis">acropolis</a>.</p>
<p>Being subjected to constant invasions and political instability, the inhabitants of the city were forced to build cell-like quarters and districts that were socially and economically independent. Each district was characterized by the religious and ethnic characteristics of its inhabitants.</p>
<p>The mainly white-stoned old town was built within the historical walls of the city, pierced by the nine historical gates, while the newer quarters of the old city were first built by the Christians during the early 15th century in the northern suburbs of the ancient city, after the Mongol withdrawal from Aleppo. The new quarters were called <i>Jdeydeh</i>. <a href="/wiki/Al-Jdayde" title="Al-Jdayde">Jdeydeh</a> is one of the finest examples of a cell-like quarter in Aleppo. After <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Tamerlane</a> invaded Aleppo in 1400 and destroyed it, the Christians migrated out of the city walls and established their own cell in 1420, at the northwestern suburbs of the city, thus founding the quarters of <a href="/wiki/Al-Jdayde" title="Al-Jdayde">Jdeydeh</a>. The inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Al-Jdayde" title="Al-Jdayde">Jdeydeh</a> were mainly brokers who facilitated trade between foreign traders and local merchants. As a result of the economic development, many other quarters were established outside the walls of the ancient city during the 15th and 16th centuries.</p>
<p>Thus, the <a href="/wiki/Old_City_of_Aleppo" class="mw-redirect" title="Old City of Aleppo">Old City of Aleppo</a> -composed of the ancient city within the walls and the old cell-like quarters outside the walls- has an approximate area of 350 hectares (1.4&#160;sq&#160;mi) housing more than 120,000 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Souqs_and_Khans">Souqs and Khans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Souqs and Khans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Al-Madina_Souq" title="Al-Madina Souq">Al-Madina Souq</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo-suq-Alp.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aleppo-suq-Alp.JPG/220px-Aleppo-suq-Alp.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aleppo-suq-Alp.JPG/330px-Aleppo-suq-Alp.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aleppo-suq-Alp.JPG/440px-Aleppo-suq-Alp.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo-suq-Alp.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ancient Aleppo, <a href="/wiki/Al-Madina_Souq" title="Al-Madina Souq">Al-Madina Souq</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city's strategic trading position attracted settlers of all races and beliefs who wished to take advantage of the commercial roads that met in Aleppo from as far as China and <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> to the east, Europe to the west, and the <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">Fertile Crescent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> to the south. The largest covered <a href="/wiki/Souq" title="Souq">souq</a>-market in the world is in Aleppo, with an approximate length of 13 kilometres (8.1 miles).<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Souq_al-Madina" class="mw-redirect" title="Souq al-Madina">Souq al-Madina</a></i>, as it is locally known, is an active trade centre for imported luxury goods, such as raw silk from <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, spices and dyes from India, and coffee from <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>. Souq al-Madina is also home to local products such as wool, agricultural products and soap. Most of the souqs date back to the 14th century and are named after various professions and crafts, hence the wool souq, the copper souq, and so on. Aside from trading, the souq accommodated the traders and their goods in <i>khans</i> (<a href="/wiki/Caravanserai" title="Caravanserai">caravanserais</a>) and scattered in the souq. Other types of small market-places were called <i>caeserias</i> (ﻗﻴﺴﺎﺭﻳﺎﺕ). Caeserias are smaller than khans in their sizes and functioned as workshops for craftsmen. Most of the khans took their names after their location in the souq and function, and are characterized with their beautiful façades and entrances with fortified wooden doors.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gates_of_Aleppo_and_other_historic_buildings">Gates of Aleppo and other historic buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Gates of Aleppo and other historic buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antioch_gate_in_Aleppo_walls.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Antioch_gate_in_Aleppo_walls.jpg/170px-Antioch_gate_in_Aleppo_walls.jpg" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Antioch_gate_in_Aleppo_walls.jpg/255px-Antioch_gate_in_Aleppo_walls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Antioch_gate_in_Aleppo_walls.jpg/340px-Antioch_gate_in_Aleppo_walls.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2283" data-file-height="3410" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antioch_gate_in_Aleppo_walls.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bab_Antakeya" title="Bab Antakeya">Gate of Antioch</a> rebuilt during the 11th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The old part of the city is surrounded with 5-kilometre-long (3.1&#160;mi), thick walls, pierced by the nine historical gates (many of them are well-preserved) of the old town. These are, clockwise from the north-east of the citadel:</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bab_al-Hadid" title="Bab al-Hadid">Bab al-Hadid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bab_al-Ahmar" title="Bab al-Ahmar">Bab al-Ahmar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bab_al-Nairab" title="Bab al-Nairab">Bab al-Nairab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bab_al-Maqam" title="Bab al-Maqam">Bab al-Maqam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bab_Qinnasrin" title="Bab Qinnasrin">Bab Qinnasrin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bab_Antakeya" title="Bab Antakeya">Bab Antakeya</a>, <a href="/wiki/B%C4%81b_Jn%C4%93n" class="mw-redirect" title="Bāb Jnēn">Bāb Jnēn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bab_al-Faraj_(Aleppo)" title="Bab al-Faraj (Aleppo)">Bab al-Faraj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bab_al-Nasr_(Aleppo)" title="Bab al-Nasr (Aleppo)">Bab al-Nasr</a>.</p>
<p>The most significant historic buildings of the ancient city include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Citadel_of_Aleppo" title="Citadel of Aleppo">The Citadel</a>, a large fortress built atop a huge, partially artificial mound rising 50&#160;m (160&#160;ft) above the city, dates back to the first millennium BC. Recent excavations unearthed a temple and 25 statues dating back to the first millennium BC.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Many of the current structures date from the 13th century. The Citadel had been extensively damaged by earthquakes, notably in 1822.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Shibani_Church" title="Al-Shibani Church">Al-Shibani Church</a>-School, <a href="/wiki/Al-Halawiyah_Madrasa" title="Al-Halawiyah Madrasa">Al-Halawiyah Madrasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Muqaddamiyah_Madrasa" title="Al-Muqaddamiyah Madrasa">Al-Muqaddamiyah Madrasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Zahiriyah_Madrasa" title="Al-Zahiriyah Madrasa">Al-Zahiriyah Madrasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Sultaniyah_Madrasa" title="Al-Sultaniyah Madrasa">Al-Sultaniyah Madrasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Firdaws_Madrasa" title="Al-Firdaws Madrasa">Al-Firdaws Madrasa</a>, Bimaristan Arghun al-Kamili, <a href="/wiki/Junblatt_Palace" title="Junblatt Palace">Junblatt Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Uthmaniyah_Madrasa" title="Al-Uthmaniyah Madrasa">Madrasa Al-Uthmaniyah</a>, Bab Al-Faraj Clock Tower, etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>The most significant historic buildings of the <a href="/wiki/Al-Jdayde" title="Al-Jdayde">Jdeydeh</a> Christian quarter include:<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><i>Beit Wakil</i>, an Aleppine mansion built in 1603, with unique wooden decorations. One of its decorations was taken to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and exhibited in <a href="/wiki/Pergamon_Museum" title="Pergamon Museum">Pergamon Museum</a>, known as the <i>Aleppo Room</i>.</li>
<li><i><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Ajikbash_House" class="extiw" title="commons:Category:Ajikbash House">Beit Achiqbash</a></i>, an old Aleppine house built in 1757. The building is home to the <i>Popular Traditions Museum</i> since 1975, showing fine decorations of the Aleppine art.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Beit_Ghazaleh" title="Beit Ghazaleh">Beit Ghazaleh</a></i>, an old 17th-century mansion characterized with fine decorations, carved by the Armenian sculptor <i>Khachadur Bali</i> in 1691. It was used as an Armenian elementary school during the 20th century.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_of_worship">Places of worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Places of worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Al-Shibani_Alp8.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Al-Shibani_Alp8.JPG/220px-Al-Shibani_Alp8.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Al-Shibani_Alp8.JPG/330px-Al-Shibani_Alp8.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Al-Shibani_Alp8.JPG/440px-Al-Shibani_Alp8.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Al-Shibani_Alp8.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Al-Shibani_Church" title="Al-Shibani Church">Al-Shibani Church</a>-School</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Aleppo" title="Great Mosque of Aleppo">Great Mosque of Aleppo</a> (Jāmi' Bani Omayya al-Kabīr), founded c. 715 by Umayyad caliph <a href="/wiki/Walid_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Walid I">Walid I</a> and most likely completed by his successor <a href="/wiki/Sulayman_ibn_Abd_al-Malik" title="Sulayman ibn Abd al-Malik">Sulayman</a>. The building contains a tomb associated with <a href="/wiki/Zechariah_(priest)" title="Zechariah (priest)">Zachary</a>, father of <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John the Baptist</a>. Construction of the present structure for Nur al-Din commenced in 1158. However, it was damaged during the <a href="/wiki/Mongol" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> invasion of 1260, and was rebuilt. The 45-metre-high (148&#160;ft) tower (described as "the principal monument of medieval Syria")<sup id="cite_ref-Burns_1999_35_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burns_1999_35-133">[133]</a></sup> was erected in 1090–1092 under the first Seljuk sultan, <a href="/wiki/Tutush_I" title="Tutush I">Tutush I</a>. It had four façades with different styles. The tower was completely destroyed during the Syrian civil war in March 2013 (reported on 24 March 2013).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Nuqtah_Mosque" title="Al-Nuqtah Mosque">Al-Nuqtah Mosque</a> ("Mosque of the drop [of blood]"), a <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shī'ah</a> mosque, which contains a stone said to be marked by a drop of <a href="/wiki/Husayn_ibn_Ali" title="Husayn ibn Ali">Husayn</a>'s blood. The site is believed to have previously been a monastery, which was converted into a mosque in 944.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Shuaibiyah_Mosque" title="Al-Shuaibiyah Mosque">Al-Shuaibiyah Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaiqan_Mosque" title="Al-Qaiqan Mosque">Al-Qaiqan Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahmandar_Mosque" title="Mahmandar Mosque">Mahmandar Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Altun_Bogha_Mosque" title="Altun Bogha Mosque">Altun Bogha Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Sahibiyah_Mosque" title="Al-Sahibiyah Mosque">Al-Sahibiyah Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahsita_Mosque" title="Bahsita Mosque">Bahsita Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Tawashi_Mosque" title="Al-Tawashi Mosque">Al-Tawashi Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Otrush_Mosque" title="Al-Otrush Mosque">Al-Otrush Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Saffahiyah_Mosque" title="Al-Saffahiyah Mosque">Al-Saffahiyah Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khusruwiyah_Mosque" title="Khusruwiyah Mosque">Khusruwiyah Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Adiliyah_Mosque" title="Al-Adiliyah Mosque">Al-Adiliyah Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahramiyah_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahramiyah Mosque">Bahramiyah Mosque</a>, etc.</li>
<li>Churches of <a href="/wiki/Al-Jdayde" title="Al-Jdayde">Jdeydeh</a> Christian quarter: the <a href="/wiki/Forty_Martyrs_Cathedral" title="Forty Martyrs Cathedral">Forty Martyrs Armenian Apostolic Cathedral</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Dormition_of_Our_Lady" title="Church of the Dormition of Our Lady">Dormition of Our Lady</a> Greek Orthodox church, <a href="/wiki/Mar_Assia_al-Hakim_Church" title="Mar Assia al-Hakim Church">Mar Assia Al-Hakim Syrian Catholic church</a>, the Maronite <a href="/wiki/Saint_Elias_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Elias Cathedral">Saint Elias Cathedral</a>, the Armenian Catholic Cathedral of Our Mother of Reliefs and the Melkite Greek Catholic Cathedral of Virgin Mary.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Synagogue_of_Aleppo" title="Central Synagogue of Aleppo">Central Synagogue of Aleppo</a> or al-Bandara synagogue, completed as early as the 9th century by the efforts of the Jewish community. The synagogue was ruined several times until 1428 when it was restored. Recently, the building was renovated by the efforts of Aleppine Jewish migrants in US.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hammams">Hammams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Hammams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hammam_Al-Nahhasseen_Aleppo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Hammam_Al-Nahhasseen_Aleppo.jpg/220px-Hammam_Al-Nahhasseen_Aleppo.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Hammam_Al-Nahhasseen_Aleppo.jpg/330px-Hammam_Al-Nahhasseen_Aleppo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Hammam_Al-Nahhasseen_Aleppo.jpg/440px-Hammam_Al-Nahhasseen_Aleppo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hammam_Al-Nahhasseen_Aleppo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hammam_al-Nahhasin" title="Hammam al-Nahhasin">Hammam al-Nahhasin</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aleppo was home to 177 <a href="/wiki/Turkish_bath" title="Turkish bath">hammams</a> during the medieval period until the Mongol invasion, when many of the prominent structures of the city were destroyed. Prior to the civil war, 18 hammams were operating in the old city, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hammam_al-Nahhasin" title="Hammam al-Nahhasin">Hammam al-Nahhasin</a> built during the 12th century near khan al-Nahhaseen.</li>
<li>Hammam al-Sultan built in 1211 by <a href="/wiki/Az-Zahir_Ghazi" title="Az-Zahir Ghazi">Az-Zahir Ghazi</a>.</li>
<li>Hammam al-Bayadah of the Mamluk era built in 1450.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hammam_Yalbugha" title="Hammam Yalbugha">Hammam Yalbugha</a> built in 1491 by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Aleppo" title="List of rulers of Aleppo">Emir of Aleppo</a> Saif ad-Din Yalbugha al-Naseri.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></li>
<li>Hammam al-Jawhary, hammam Azdemir, hammam Bahram Pasha, hammam Bab al-Ahmar, etc.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nearby_attractions_and_the_Dead_Cities">Nearby attractions and the <i>Dead Cities</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Nearby attractions and the Dead Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dead_Cities" title="Dead Cities">Dead Cities</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kharab_Shams_Basilica,_Dead_Cities_region,_NW_Syria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kharab_Shams_Basilica%2C_Dead_Cities_region%2C_NW_Syria.jpg/220px-Kharab_Shams_Basilica%2C_Dead_Cities_region%2C_NW_Syria.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kharab_Shams_Basilica%2C_Dead_Cities_region%2C_NW_Syria.jpg/330px-Kharab_Shams_Basilica%2C_Dead_Cities_region%2C_NW_Syria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kharab_Shams_Basilica%2C_Dead_Cities_region%2C_NW_Syria.jpg/440px-Kharab_Shams_Basilica%2C_Dead_Cities_region%2C_NW_Syria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1967" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kharab_Shams_Basilica,_Dead_Cities_region,_NW_Syria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kharab Shams Basilica</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aleppo's western suburbs are home to a group of historical sites and villages which are commonly known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Dead_Cities" title="Dead Cities">Dead Cities</a></i>. Around 700 abandoned settlements in the northwestern parts of Syria prior to the 5th century, contain remains of Christian <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">Byzantine architecture</a>. Many hundreds of those settlements are located in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Simeon" title="Mount Simeon">Mount Simeon</a> (Jabal Semaan) and Jabal Halaqa regions at the western suburbs of Aleppo, within the range of <a href="/wiki/Limestone_Massif" title="Limestone Massif">Limestone Massif</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Dead Cites were inscribed as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> in 2011, under the name of "Ancient Villages of Northern Syria".<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most notable <i>Dead cities</i> and archaeological sites in Mount Simeon and <a href="/wiki/Kurd_Mountain" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurd Mountain">Mount Kurd</a> near Aleppo include: the Kalota Castle and churches northwest of Aleppo, the Kharab Shams Byzantine basilica of the 4th century,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> the half-ruined Roman basilica in Fafertin village of 372 AD, the old Byzantine settlement of Surqanya village northwest of Aleppo, the 4th-century Basilic church of Sinhar historic settlement, the Mushabbak Basilica dating back to the second half of the 5th century, the 9th-century BC Assyrian settlement of Kafr Nabo, <a href="/wiki/Barad,_Syria" title="Barad, Syria">Brad</a> village and the <a href="/wiki/Julian_of_Antioch" title="Julian of Antioch">Saint Julianus</a> Maronite monastery (399–402 AD) where the shrine of <a href="/wiki/Maron" title="Maron">Saint Maron</a> is located, the 5th-century Kimar settlement of the Roman and Byzantine eras, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint_Simeon_Stylites" title="Church of Saint Simeon Stylites">Church of Saint Simeon Stylites</a> of the 5th century, the <a href="/wiki/Syro%E2%80%93Hittite_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Syro–Hittite states">Syro-Hittite</a> <a href="/wiki/Ain_Dara_temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Ain Dara temple">Ain Dara temple</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> dating back to the 10th and 8th centuries BC, the ancient city of <a href="/wiki/Cyrrhus" title="Cyrrhus">Cyrrhus</a> with the old Roman amphitheatre and two historic bridges, etc.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses_and_minibuses">Buses and minibuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Buses and minibuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city of Aleppo is served by a <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a> network of buses and minibuses. New modern buses are used to connect the city with Damascus and the other Syrian cities to the east and the south of Aleppo.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_Bagdad_Railway_Station,_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Aleppo_Bagdad_Railway_Station%2C_cropped.jpg/220px-Aleppo_Bagdad_Railway_Station%2C_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Aleppo_Bagdad_Railway_Station%2C_cropped.jpg/330px-Aleppo_Bagdad_Railway_Station%2C_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Aleppo_Bagdad_Railway_Station%2C_cropped.jpg/440px-Aleppo_Bagdad_Railway_Station%2C_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1388" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_Bagdad_Railway_Station,_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Aleppo_Railway_Station" title="Aleppo Railway Station">Aleppo Railway Station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aleppo was one of the major stations of Syria that has been connected with the <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Railway" title="Baghdad Railway">Baghdad Railway</a> in 1912, within the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. The connections to Turkey and onwards to <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a> still exist today, with a twice weekly train from Damascus. It is perhaps for this historical reason that Aleppo is the headquarters of Syria national railway network, <a href="/wiki/Chemins_de_Fer_Syriens" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemins de Fer Syriens">Chemins de Fer Syriens</a>. As the railway is relatively slow, much of the passenger traffic to the port of <a href="/wiki/Latakia" title="Latakia">Latakia</a> had moved to road-based air-conditioned coaches. But this has reversed in recent years with the 2005 introduction of South Korean built <a href="/wiki/Diesel_multiple_unit" title="Diesel multiple unit">DMUs</a> providing a regular bi-hourly express service to both Latakia and Damascus, which miss intermediate stations.</p>
<p>However, after the break-out of the civil war in 2011, the Syrian railway network has suffered major damage and is currently out of use.</p>
<p>The opening scene in <a href="/wiki/Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie">Agatha Christie</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Murder_on_the_Orient_Express" title="Murder on the Orient Express">Murder on the Orient Express</a></i> takes place on the railway station in Aleppo: "It was five o'clock on a winter's morning in Syria. Alongside the platform at Aleppo stood the train grandly designated in railway guides as the Taurus Express."</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_(2)_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Aleppo_%282%29_cropped.jpg/260px-Aleppo_%282%29_cropped.jpg" width="260" height="92" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Aleppo_%282%29_cropped.jpg/390px-Aleppo_%282%29_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Aleppo_%282%29_cropped.jpg/520px-Aleppo_%282%29_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2794" data-file-height="990" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_(2)_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Aleppo_International_Airport" title="Aleppo International Airport">Aleppo International Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Aleppo_International_Airport" title="Aleppo International Airport">Aleppo International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA" class="mw-redirect" title="IATA">IATA</a>: ALP, <a href="/wiki/ICAO" class="mw-redirect" title="ICAO">ICAO</a>: OSAP) is the international airport serving the city. The airport serves as a secondary hub for <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Arab_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian Arab Airlines">Syrian Arab Airlines</a>. The history of the airport dates back to the beginning of the 20th century. It was upgraded and developed in the years to 1999 when the new current terminal was opened.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>The airport was closed since the beginning of 2013 as a result of the military operations in the area. However, following the Syrian government's recapture of eastern Aleppo during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aleppo_(2012%E2%80%9316)" title="Battle of Aleppo (2012–16)">Battle of Aleppo</a>, an airplane conducted its first flight from the airport in four years. The flight, conducted on 5 January 2017, was a trial attempt by the government before the airport fully opens to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_and_industry">Trade and industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Trade and industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo,_textile_suq_market.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Aleppo%2C_textile_suq_market.jpg/220px-Aleppo%2C_textile_suq_market.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Aleppo%2C_textile_suq_market.jpg/330px-Aleppo%2C_textile_suq_market.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Aleppo%2C_textile_suq_market.jpg/440px-Aleppo%2C_textile_suq_market.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo,_textile_suq_market.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Traditional textile and rug markets</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main role of the city was as a trading place throughout the history, as it sat at the crossroads of two trade routes and mediated the trade from India, the <a href="/wiki/Tigris" title="Tigris">Tigris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euphrates" title="Euphrates">Euphrates</a> regions and the route coming from <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a> in the South, which traced the base of the mountains rather than the rugged seacoast. Although trade was often directed away from the city for political reasons<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="(January 2012)">why?</span></a></i>]</sup>, it continued to thrive until the Europeans began to use the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape route</a> to India and later to utilize the route through <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>.</p>
<p>The commercial traditions in Aleppo have deep roots in the history. The Aleppo Chamber of commerce founded in 1885, is one of the oldest chambers in the Middle East and the Arab world. According to many historians, Aleppo was the most developed commercial and industrial city in the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> after <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_the_Ottoman_Empire-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_shopping_street.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aleppo_shopping_street.jpg/220px-Aleppo_shopping_street.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aleppo_shopping_street.jpg/330px-Aleppo_shopping_street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aleppo_shopping_street.jpg/440px-Aleppo_shopping_street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo_shopping_street.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Markets at Tilel street</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the largest urban area in pre-civil war Syria, the economy of Aleppo is driven by textiles, chemicals, pharmaceutics, agro-processing industries, electrical commodities, alcoholic beverages, engineering and tourism. It is the country's dominant manufacturing centre, with a share of more than 50% of manufacturing employment and an even greater export share.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Possessing the most developed commercial and industrial plants in Syria, Aleppo is a major centre for manufacturing precious metals and stones.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> The annual amount of the processed gold produced in Aleppo is around 8.5 tonnes, making up to 40% of the entire manufactured gold in Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>The industrial city of Aleppo in <a href="/wiki/Shaykh_Najjar" title="Shaykh Najjar">Sheikh Najjar</a> district is one of the largest in Syria and the region. Occupying an area of 4,412 hectares (10,900 acres) in the north-eastern suburbs of Aleppo, the total investments in the city counted more than US$3.4 billion during 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Still under development, it is envisaged to open hotels, exhibition centres and other facilities within the industrial city.</p>
<p>The old traditional crafts are well-preserved in the old part of the city. The famous laurel <a href="/wiki/Aleppo_soap" title="Aleppo soap">soap of Aleppo</a> is considered to be the world's first hard soap.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AleppoCitadel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/AleppoCitadel.jpg/220px-AleppoCitadel.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/AleppoCitadel.jpg/330px-AleppoCitadel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/AleppoCitadel.jpg/440px-AleppoCitadel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2950" data-file-height="2212" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AleppoCitadel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The restored square of the citadel</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aleppo is one of the fastest-growing cities in Syria and the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Many villagers and inhabitants of other Syrian districts are migrating to Aleppo in an effort to find better job opportunities, a fact that always increases population pressure, with a growing demand for new residential capacity. New districts and residential communities have been built in the suburbs of Aleppo, many of them are still under construction as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.</p>
<p>Two major construction projects are scheduled in Aleppo: the "Old City Revival" project and the "Reopening of the stream bed of Queiq River".</p>
<ul>
<li>The Old City revival project completed its first phase by the end of 2008, and the second phase started in early 2010. The purpose of the project is the preservation of the old city of Aleppo with its souqs and khans, and restoration of the narrow alleys of the old city and the roads around the citadel.</li>
<li>The restoration of <a href="/wiki/Queiq_River" title="Queiq River">Queiq River</a> is directed towards the revival of the flow of the river, demolishing both the artificial cover of the stream bed and the reinforcement of the stream banks along the river in the city centre. The flow of the river was blocked during the 1960s by the Turks, turning the river into a tiny sewage channel, something that led the authorities to cover the stream during the 1970s. In 2006 the flow of pure water was restored through the efforts of the Syrian government, granting a new life to the Quweiq River.</li>
</ul>
<p>Like other major Syrian cities, Aleppo is suffering from the dispersal of <a href="/wiki/Informal_settlements" class="mw-redirect" title="Informal settlements">informal settlements</a>: almost half of its population (around 1.2 million) is estimated to live in 22 informal settlements of different types.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leisure_and_entertainment">Leisure and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleppo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Leisure and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
